Ions such as cations (e.g., Na⁺, K⁺, metal ions) and anions (e.g., Cl⁻, SO₄²⁻) also commonly act as guests, especially in ionophore systems. Biomolecules like amino acids, peptides, and nucleotides can serve as guests in biological host systems like cyclodextrins or protein cavities. These guest molecules are characterized by their ability to form non-covalent interactions—hydrogen bonds, π-π stacking, van der Waals forces, and electrostatic interactions—with the host molecules. These guest molecules are characterized by their ability to form non-covalent interactions—hydrogen bonds, π-π stacking, van der Waals forces, and electrostatic interactions—with the host molecules.
